There is almost no strategy involved. But, if you are looking for a mindless, fantasy themed game to play with the family this one is perfect for that!

RATING: 7.9
I had never played Talisman until this new (Black Industries) 4th edition. Read many things about it and was familiar with the basics of game play.
 
Pros: They did a beautiful job with the overall graphics. The board is attractive and a nice size plus lots of helpful text (when correct- more later). The 2-D character pieces are also very nice and I don't really mind them over 3-D plastic pieces (especially if not painted). The cards have nice images and readable text. The game play is pretty much what you'd expect from a game designed originally in the early 80's. There's definitely some player tension and I probably would have seen more tension had we all had some previous hands-on experience with the game.

Cons: Errors?  Yes, lots of errors. People are already pointing out incorrect character card text (Prophetess). There is at least one board printing error and possibly more depending on the ruling on the Village and City spaces. The rulebook is ill conceived so much so that it's hard to find answers to obvious questions. Yes, the little plastic pieces used to record Strength, Craft, and Life were also ill conceived. I'd probably take a paint pen to them and color the number so that it stood out at the very least. The cards (and box) are not "Euro-Quality" and Chinese printing (though probably cheaper) doesn't reach that same quality level.  Also, I would have expected a few more variant/optional rules included as the game has gone through several editions with lots of tweaks. 

Overall, the game still has a charm to it that is undeniable. Fixing some of the errors is an obvious first step. And I think a few advanced rules could kick the strategy quotient up a bit without doing any damage to the core game. 

**Update 1-8-09**

As I now have the new revised 4th edition by FFG and played a session, I've upped my overall rating. Mainly because of the following:

* They cleaned up the board, rules, and card language to make it more consistent. There's very few errors (only spotted one so far).

* I love the plastic minis as they lend a much nicer look to the game. I look forward to painting them. :)

* I like the little cones for the craft, strength, and life tokens. Much easier to pick up and count.

* I think the Fate tokens are a very good addition to the system. This addition helps to balance some of the bad luck that players sometimes get in spades.

The game can still run long but it is a fun adventure game experience. This is a true board game classic.

RATING: 10
Chaotic, crazy, fantasy-themed fun! This new edition looks really nice, with the cool gold coins, awesome board and card art, and little plastic pieces for stats (I'm just using all of them for '1'). Great "experience" game with little downtime and lots of variety. Also, the gameplay is light enough that pretty much anyone can join in and have fun.

At first glance, there doesn't seem to be much choice or opportunity for strategy (just roll a die, move that many, draw a card and do what it says), but there's a bit more decision making than people give it credit for. You feel like you are both choosing your own adventure and simply going along with the story. Still, there isn't [i]a lot[/i] of strategy here, and this is a nice game to play when you want some light fun after a long day. (I wrote more about the important decisions you make during the game here: http://www.boardgamegeek.com/thread/438714)

Fate is a nice addition to the game. It cuts down on play time and frustration from unlucky die rolls, plus it sort of balances the characters (characters with crappy abilities get more fate).

Wow, my rating for this game continues to increase as I play it more and more. This game is ALL KINDS OF AWESOME.

RATING: 9
Player interaction: race, take-that, dice based combat.

Themes: adventure, there can be only one, fantasy quest.

Components: Art ranges from conventional (cards) to ugly (board). Plastic components are nice.

A game where anything can happen.  This is sword and sorcery pulp fiction in board game form.  Though the rules are simple you never know what random monster is going to show up around the next bend.  There is a general structure to the flow of the game.  Players strive to become strong enough to enter the center of the board and kill their opponents.  The board is divided into various regions and each have their own feel.  This heightens the joy of exploration and provides the players with strategic direction.

Talisman is the best adventure game designed so far and the FFG printing is the best version.  (I do wish FFG would get their artists to redo the board.  The Black Industries art is bland.  And now that I've seen Relic, I'm even more interested in an update to the Talisman board.)

RATING: 3
Very rarely, a few times in a lifetime, you play a game and when you finish it nothing can ever be the same. Walls have been pulled down, barriers broken, a dimension of feeling, of existence itself, has opened in you that was not there before. Talisman is a game of this magnitude. John Goodenough may be the most gifted designer in the industry; gifted not just because of his imagination, his energy, his originality, but because he has access to the unutterable, because he can look inside a person and discover the unique essence of his humanity. For years he has been designing games about what it means to defend this essence, this unique light, against a world designed to extinguish it. Talisman is his most powerful, shattering, and unflinching story of this defense. To read it is to have yourself taken apart, undone, touched at the place of your own essence; it is to be turned back, as if after a long absence, into a human being.

RATING: 9
[2-6] While many people despise this game, I'm pretty fond of the era of gaming it represents. Simple rules, ridiculous outcomes, and kitschy fantasy adventures. It feels so 1980s in the way that it represents a nostalgic throwback to the epic late nights of pizza, soda, and yelling friends. Sure, there's not much strategy but the beauty of gaming is that good game experiences don't have to be strategic. Talisman is trashy fun. Period.

Expansions owned: [thing=121786]Blood Moon[/thing]; [thing=38025]Reaper[/thing]; [thing=41064]Dungeon[/thing]; [thing=131816]The City[/thing]; [thing=152319]Nether Realm[/thing]; [thing=169254]Deep Realms[/thing]; [thing=177211]The Harbinger[/thing]

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
I enjoyed playing this back in the 90s. However I really enjoy the new Revised 4th edition today as well. I usually house rule a few things to speed up the play (+stats every 6 points, +1 stat every 4 turns, use fate for moving extra spaces, etc.). It's a much an adventure as a game. I have some amazing memories of games: 1) Playing on my birthday a few years ago and my daughter got to the crown, held off her brother, then I got there and was weak but used a healing trinket to re-heal over and over and over and finally it came down to one roll and she won, epic! 2) Playing on my son's 16th birthday where he held off my friend an I to barely win in the end, epic as well!. If you need a game where you can strategize to win then avoid this. This is random and luck filled and yet great. There's nothing like it. Don't play to 'win', instead play to laugh, tell stories, and have fun!

RATING: 10
Releasing the 4th edition really says all about this game. It's one of the easiest games to get into. Even though it's very detailed. And most of the questions encountered is answered in the short, but informative guide.

I can't give it anything less than 10. Easy to get into. Unique way of building a world.  And you can't be eliminated before the endgame. Even though it's hard starting all over when it's close to the endgame. The mechanics are easy. No fiddling about with a lot of different stats. It's just strenght and craft. And items either raising them or gives you a dice throw to save a life. Couldn't be any simpler.

RATING: 9.5
Talisman will never win awards for game design, being high on luck, low on strategy.  There IS room for tactics and lots of decisions, but ultimately the chaos and variety are what make this game.  With the right group of people, Talisman is great fun and makes a virtue of being unbalanced, with wild swings of fortune.  Talisman allows more variety of playing styles than many games - yes, you can go for the win, but you can also have a great time just accumulating goodies, becoming super-powerful or frustrating your opponents.

RATING: 9
Very enjoyable, time consuming game. Put on the coffee pot and stoke the pipe. It's gonna be a loooong night.
Now that I own this game, I have created a single player style where I use 2 characters ( the troll and the assassin)as the chasers and 2 characters (either random or the warrior and the dwarf) as the ones that have to try to get to the crown. The chasers have to try to kill the 2 that are trying to get to the crown. Game plays basically the same as a normal game except that the chasers do not need a raft to cross the river and do not need to fight the sentinel.

RATING: N/A
Good game. For an old guy, I found the board not as easy to read as the second edition. That being said, the art is excellent, the quality of the components far exceeds the second edition. The rules streamline the play. As you can increase the maximum number of lives, it is easier to get to the crown of command relatively intact. The only downside compared to the second edition was the lack of expansions - I am used to the greater variability of characters, draws from the adventure deck and the expansions themselves, etc. The first time we played the game we went throught e adventure deck twice. We've never done that with the second edition game, even with nine players. 

The simple base game is simply simpler. When we want to play a more complex game with more variability, we play the second edition, when we want an easier game with better esthetics, we play the fourth edition. We are awaiting the possible expansions for this latest version.

RATING: 8
Really good adventure board game when playing with 4 or more players.

Then it will be very entertaining and fast-paced. It also creates a nice atmosphere at the table.

A true "feel-good" boardgame with the right group! Nonetheless the game mechanics are kind of old (roll and move) and it can drag very long.

EDIT 2016: Talisman is a special game. When I start playing thematic games I liked the game quite a bit. After bying more and more expansions and mixed that in the fun was going away because - yes - it is very (too) random and it can drag on forever when playing with the expansions. 

Last week I played it again with only the base board and I rediscovered what I liked about it. Not the mechanics (are there any mechanics in Talsiman?) make it a nice game - it is the flow of play and the thematic atmosphere. You can like Talisman if you take it not that seriously. Next time I want to play with only one big board expansion mixed in.

RATING: 6
I never played Talisman as a kid, but if I had, my brothers and I would no doubt have spent entire days sprawled around this game on the floor of the lounge. Yes, it's silly, it's unfair, it scales poorly, it's hugely reliant on the luck of the dice. But there's something in it that just sparks the imagination, as each card drawn adds a tiny detail to your hero's story, a glorious song of vanquished foes and endless treasure, or a tale of woe in which bandits steal your gold, a poltegeist haunts you incessantly, and a witch turns you into a toad. In another life I could see myself buying EVERY EXPANSION and luxuriating in the glorious vastness of it all, but I know that sort of money (and shelf space) could get me a dozen other (better) games.

RATING: 9
Let me start by saying, "I love this game"! I have been a huge fan of the franchise since the 2nd edition.  I never played the 3rd ed. and kept playing with the older 2nd.  This 4th ed. blew me away the second I opened the box.  The board is huge and the graphics on both the board and the cards are a massive improvement to the earlier versions.  I love the cones and very happy to see the contents appear to be more sturdy than the 2nd ed.  What I like about the game is how easily it plays.  It is a simple RPG, character builder game with dice rolls and modifiers. I can enjoy it with my 8 yo and with new players too.  I noticed after a few plays that some of the nuances of the 2nd ed. were corrected in subtle tweaks in the rules/mechanics.  Just as I did with the 2nd ed, I plan to obtain as many of the expansions as I can get my hands on.

[b]Update[/b] - The very same comment above has been more than enough a reason during my Fall 2015 rating revise to lower my rating from an excessive 8 to a more fitting 4, that better mirrors what now I’m growing toward all dungeon crawls.

RATING: 1
Talisman is a Chinese water torture. It is the death of a thousand cuts. It is the stone of Sisyphus, a calliope of boredom. It's the first 5 seconds of each day from Groundhog Day. It's the steaming charred mass in the toaster oven at the end of Time Bandits. Talisman is the science teacher from The Wonder Years without any filmstrips. It's neither a floor wax nor a dessert topping. It's a mirage in the desert, a black widow crawling up your chest. It's a female preying mantis and you're it's mate. It's a stale box of Crackerjacks without a toy surprise. Talisman is the Night of the Living Dead, the Dark Side of the Force. It's the Energizer bunny gone hideously awry. It's that dream where you're running as fast as you can but you're not going anywhere and when you open your mouth to scream, nothing comes out. Talisman is a naked singularity, an event horizon from which fun cannot escape. It's a souffle that never rose, the fault-ridden pudding skin in the back of the fridge. Talisman is Xeno's worst nightmare.

RATING: 6.5
Algunos lo denominan la oca friki. Y la descripción es bastante acertada. El tablero consiste en tres pistas concentricas y en cada casilla pueden surgir retos y cartas que cambian las propiedades de la casilla y tal. Cada jugador lleva un personaje con ciertas características (fate, gold, strength, craft) y a medida que avanza el juego puede ir recogiendo objetos o ganando experiencia y aumentando sus características. El objetivo es llegar a la casilla central, desde donde se pueden lanzar rayos para eliminar a los contrincantes. 
Es un juego sencillo de mecánicas, pero con numerosisismas cartas que hacen que cada partida sea un mundo. Es completamente caótico. En cualquier momento un mal evento o una mala tirada, puede echar a perder toda una trayectoria de mejora del personaje... así con todo, puede resultar divertido.

La pega que le veo es que es bastante largo de jugar. Para esa duración (sólo he jugado una partida a seis, inconclusa, que duró cuatro horas), hay mejores opciones. Es un juego sin pretensiones.. para pasar el rato, putear al prójimo y probar qué tal suerte tienes con los dados.

Es muy conocido.. y hay muchísimas expansiones. Van por la cuarta edición.

RATING: 8
Talisman was really my first step into designer board games. I played it and liked it, but once I got a taste of the games that followed (Arkham Horror, Runebound, Descent, RoboRally), Talisman began to lose luster for me. It seemed flat, random and uninteresting. THEN, Fantasy Flight acquired the game, made some excellent revisions and unleashed two expansions that provided rocket fuel to my affection for this game. The Dungeon Expansion, in particular, adds depth and nostalgic flavor to this game.

Without the expansions, I'd probably rate the initial 4E Talisman a 7 and the revised FF 4E an 8. But *with* the expansions (and there's no reason not to play all of them all the time), this game is classic. It has caused me to completely re-evaluate my Top 10.

RATING: 9
I really had a blast playing Talisman. As should be obvious, this is not a game that your megagamer winwinwinnner types are likely to enjoy. It's pure, dumb, thematic fun. Still, it isn't totally strategy-free. Deciding in which direction to head and when are really important. So is deciding for how long  you can push your luck and build up your strength on the outer tracks before one of the other players beats you to the crown. Is the games super-deep or offering myriad decisions? No, but what exactly are you expecting from a thematic roll-and-move that nearly anyone (save ubergamer snobs) will enjoy?

As as usual with FFG, the art is not so great and it is overproduced and has those crappy small cards, but for once I didn't mind. Talisman was a great property for FFG to pick up and I'm grateful that they did.

RATING: 7
A significant improvement from the 3rd Edition.  I never owned the 2nd Ed, but did play a few times back in my college days.  Any comparisons to 2nd Ed won't be accurate due to memory loss.

I enjoy this game much more than the last iteration.  The fact that a player wins when everyone else dies (rather than after beating the Dragon King) is much more pleasing.  It speeds up game play if you play with agressive players, and encourages more player interaction as it is more likely that characters will want to encounter other characters on a space, rather than encountering the space.  I also like the third "inner" ring that is missing on the 3rd edition.  The Raft cards make for a great way to get across the river, and the corner buildings are better.  Gold also flows more freely.  The spells are also better, and make playing a spellcaster much more pleasing.

My only gripe with this edition is the glossy, almost "sticky" nature of the cards.  It forces them to stick together, and when combined with their annoyingly small size, makes shuffling very difficult.

Overall, though a great game - nicely harkens back to what I remember about the 2nd Ed from 20 years ago.

EDIT:  Gave it to my friend as a "House Warming Gift" when he finally moved out of his parents basement and got an apartment.  Which is fine, as I intend to obtain the forthcoming FFG reprint.

EDIT:  Have finally reacquired Talisman - this time, it's the FFG Revised 4th.  I like it better.  Better rulebook, better plastic mini's, better cards.  Better everything.

RATING: 7
As I'm probably the Talisman expert of our growing group, having grown up with it, I like to describe it as the only game we have access to where the gameplay is "roll the dice, land on a square, draw a card, and do what it says." Isn't that what all games were like back in the day? It seems so rare to still see now. The Talisman franchise does this all with flair, and multiple decks each the side of your head. My sense of time must be affected by nostalgia, because the newbies always tell me the game runs too long. I'll take their word for it. If you don't mind an even longer game, play with *all* the expansions: each attaches to one corner of the board. If you want a more grown up version, you'll find a near exact but enhanced version called Relic.

RATING: 10
We simply can't stop playing this game! Epic struggle for the Crown of Command. Many early memories about RPGs and classic fantasy books (for example Titan by Livingstone and Jackson) have come up since Talisman is the part of my collection of boardgames. 

Update on 8 August, 2012.
Having purchased a few of the expansions like the Highland, the Dungeon, the Frostmarch and the Sacred Pool this game is even more entertaining than before.
The pile of Adventure cards is so tall that we play with our own house rule for this: after shuffling this deck very much, we usually create 2-4 decks from it (depending on the number of players). Ideally every player has its own deck of adventure cards. Besides this ways it gets easier to handle so many Adventure cards, this also symbolizes fate or determination in the game. 
Of course, decreasing the number of adventure cards before playing could be a solution, but we don't want to select certain cards while leave out others.

Update on 24 November, 2013.
Having purchased all of the expansions, my collection is complete, at least until the next expansion.
I sorted out all the adventure cards of the base game because of their generic nature. This way we only use the adventure cards from the expansions. The adventure deck is still huge and hard to handle properly, but it does worth the effort! :D


Update on July 31st, 2015
My 4th revised edition Talisman collection seems to be complete. I just keep repeating myself, but this is an amazing game if you play it with expansions. The Blood Moon, the Dragon, the Woodland etc. all expansions are well integrated into the base game and make it something different and something variable. We almost always play the game with the hidden ending variant which keeps the excitement high. 
Although the base game can be easily regarded as a roll and move type of a simple game, with expansions it really begins to shine as a complex game where you have more options than just deciding which way to go on the board.  
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
OK, I'll tell you up front that the supposed "discerning" gamers who bitch and moan about the luck/randomness/chaos in TALISMAN or the assumption that the game lacks "meaningful choices" (whatever that means in the context of a f&%king board game)just don't get it.  They never will, and for those Days of Wonder shills, middle managers, and spreadsheet fanatics there's plenty of games out there to satisfy their desire to amoritize, impress, and bid their way to victory.  Make no mistake- the 4th edition of TALISMAN will not make you a believer if you didn't like it to begin with, nor should it because it is first and foremost a return of the classic 2nd edition of the game which has not, contrary to some opinions here, become "dated" or "aged poorly". Nor is the appeal of the game somehow limited to some hazy sense of nostalgia.  In fact, having not played the base game without expansions, I was really amazed at how good a game TALISMAN really is- even with THE CITY, DUNGEON, TIMESCAPE, et. al. stripped away.  It's simple, almost elemental, and definitely classical.  But dated?  That's like saying that Johnny Cash records are dated.  No- it doesn't feature the currently in-vogue mechanics and it's not one of these oh-so-clever minimalist Eurogames where the designer's goal was to abstract everything interesting away to a simple flowchart.  But that doesn't make it any less vital, exciting, and fun, then it was when I played it for the first time nearly 20 years ago.  What's more significant is that returning to TALISMAN made me realize that a lot of what's missing in games today is a real sense of character, a palpable heart and soul that makes the game truly unique.  Even amongst games like TALISMAN inspired games like PROPHECY or FFG's fantasy titles, TALISMAN stands out as something singular in the hobby that has proven over the past 25 years to be a timeless, perennial game that will likely be played and enjoyed long after the faddish games that litter the hobby now are long forgotten.  Fortunately, this is also the best produced edition of TALISMAN to date although I do  miss the old GW-style artwork but it's a beautiful set that manages to capture baroque 1980s-style fantasy with modern production values in a very classy package.  Black Industries has really got their work cut out for them now- I'm already ready for the expansions!

RATING: 3
I've owned this game for roughly seven years. I've played it about five to six times in all that time. Every now and then someone is like "hey, we haven't played Talisman in ages and I'd like to play it even though I have a faint memory it is not very good" to which everyone else replies "sure, why not, let's give it a chance, I have a few cans of beer ready and my dice hand itches".

This is followed by roughly two to three hours of frantic dice throwing after which everyone comes to the conclusion that this game can't be won in any reasonable time and it's extremely boring. After this we bury the game box in the deep of the night into the flower bed in my back yard until it's time for it to do it's yearly manifestation again.

Seriously. In this game you just throw the die and hope you can do something good with the result. Wait for everyone else to do the same and then it's your turn again. No serious planning or anything like that. Too random. It would be ok if the playtime was under an hour, but in our hands the game always ends up lasting an eternity. Maybe we are just too good or conservative in keeping our characters alive?

RATING: 8
I know everyone hates roll and move, and everyone hates too much randomness in their games, and for that reason a lot of people hate Talisman, I can't help it I just find I really enjoy this game.

The theme really draws me in, there aren't many games of this ilk (or not many stand-out games). There are plenty of dungeon crawlers but how many games outside of RPGs let you wander strange lands meeting strange characters and having high adventure along the way?

In its fourth edition now the quality really shows. The artwork is superb. The miniatures are works of art in themselves (sure you can find better miniatures elsewhere, but very few boardgames have miniatures of this quality and level of detail).

Roll and move can get frustrating but Talisman at least lets you choose between two destinations, and in the end game it lets you have more control over your movement. You can always house rule two dice for movement and pick one if you want more control, personally it bugs me less in this game than it does elsewhere, I'm not sure why, probably because it forces me into choices I wouldn't have made and that often leads to epic battles or unexpected treasure troves.

Equal parts rewarding and punishing (nobody wants to be turned into a toad three turns before they capture the crown of command), one thing I really enjoy is that it's difficult to come up with an overarching strategy that lets one player dominate. Picking random characters and the randomness inherent in some much of the game, from the movement to the adventure cards to the expanded end conditions in the expansions, means you're always thinking on your feet and it's one game where newbies are not severely disadvantaged when going up against seasoned players.

Game length can run ridiculously long, especially if players are afraid to commit to an early run to the middle, but so long as you account for this (and make sure beers and snacks are in plentiful supply) that's not necessarily a negative, but it might affect how often you get this to the table.

RATING: 8.5
I have a special place in my heart for this game.  I first played Talisman back in 2003.  A friend of mine owned an older version of the game and we used to play occasionally.  This was the game that made me realize that there are other board games out there.  Up to that point I had only played the mass produced games that permeate most shelves in a home, like Monopoly, Balderdash, and many others.

Talisman opened me to a whole new world of board games and to this day remains as one of my favorites.  It is a heavy game and can take quite some time to play, but that's one of the things I like about it.  Whenever I play this game I feel fully immersed in the story and take on the role of the character I'm playing.  There are very few games out there that have done this for me.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Whant can I say about a Board Game that has been around for 30 years and is still going strong? It's a Legacy in and off itself and in my opinion the best Fantasy themed Game out there, that entertains for hours in a session.

The Rules are simple and very easy to understand, the components are absolutely gorgeous with some neat Artwork and nice plastic miniatures. The replayability because of its randomness is huge and especially with 1 or 2 Expansions no Game will EVER be the same.

Some hardcore Gamers will not like the Game because so many things are made random by card drwaing and expecially dice rolling, but that is the fun of it and makes it more easy to play. If someone wants to play a longer game, but is intimidated by the Rules or strategy aspect (like in Arkham Horror) they may prefer Talisman.

In my opinion, this is one of the best and most influential Games ever made and I will play it as often as I can for years to come.

RATING: 8
Talisman is a blast!  I played with my wife and we soon realized two things:  First and foremost, playing with more than two people would greatly increase the amount of tension and competition in this game.  Second, it does NOT take as much preparation to go for the game's main quest goal as we originally thought.

Our playthrough lasted about two hours, but once my wife got to the innermost circle of the board, she pretty much just walked right up to the end goal.  

There is a good amount of luck-of-the-dice involved with this game, which is normally a turn off for me in RPG settings, but the simplicity of the rules and the beauty of the artwork makes it an asset as opposed to a deficit.  Reason being, a game like this is perfect as a stepping stone from casual games to heavy games.  There are plenty of elements you would find in a heavier game, but they are very simple and not at all overwhelming.  

The combination of this with the luck-of-the-dice aspects means that even a player new to board games has more than just a slim chance of winning.  This is great for their growth into the board gaming community and could be the difference between a bad night and the start of a new hobby.

Definitely recommend bringing this game out at a board game night with a new player and have your goal be to help fend off the other players to give them a fighting chance.

I can see myself pulling this out for years when I want a light, fun dice chucking adventure.

RATING: 5
The newest edition of Talisman, from Fantasy Flight.  Having owned the first (B/W), second (colour) and third (skulls!) editions from Games Workshop over the years, I picked this up to play with my son.  Overall, it's the same old Talisman, with some slightly different spaces on the board, and a new Fate (re-roll) mechanic.  The character card art on the new edition is junky, but the art in the decks looks nice, and the cards seem sturdy.  Talisman is what it is, a random adventure luck-fest - control freaks will hate it, but for a family game, it's a gem.

RATING: 9
Beautiful production of the classic adventure game. One of the best looking game BOARDS I own. It's important to recognize that this is more of an adventure game than a strategy game.  It reminds me of the old "Choose Your Own Adventure" books with the path options you can take.  Tremendously unpredictable, with some funny coincidences.  There is a wee bit of strategy, however, in terms of timing your push for the Crown.  Light, luck-filled and can be long, but has proven to be an excellent game to play with younger gamers as well.  To enjoy this game, you have to accept it for what it *is* rather than berate it for what it *isn't*.  The game certainly has a very strong identity and character to it.  It's pretty inspired in that way.  We always have fun playing it, and that's the bottom line.

RATING: 1
Some people might find it odd that I rate this so low when I enjoy Dungeonquest so much. The difference between these two games is that where Dungeonquest randomly punishes everyone, this game randomly punishes OR rewards them. So one player might be stuck as a toad forever, which would be hilarious if the other players were subject to similar drawbacks. But no.

The game is frustrating to lose because someone else is being randomly rewarded while you're being punished. And it's frustrating to win because there's always going to be someone at the table who's grumpy about being hosed. I've been in both positions, and neither are fun.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Game looks so much more awesome on the table than the actual experience.  I love how the board fits in with the expansions' add ons.  It's a gorgeous presentation.  
Still, I haven't played this in a while until Dec 2017.  The experience was okay, but there are so many better fantasy titles to play for complexity and narrative.  One of the biggest issues I felt during this last play through was the roll and move - and whatever you roll you must move.  I'm thinking I'm going to allow a character to move up to their rolled number to allow a bit more flexibility in what they do and where they go.  It will prevent this back and forth movement while trying to land on a specific space.  Truly, allowing movement to be more flexible will quicken the game and add more choice to your rolls.  Character combat will increase (knowing the people who play this game) and your ability to not walk by items or spaces that could benefit you is also eliminated.  
Might also try the idea that you can't move past monsters who are already on the board.
Games a 6/7 at best.  Some modifications will aid in its play.

RATING: 5.8
Massive text reading.  Every stop on the read requires reading & the board is so large, if my piece was on the other side of the board had to have the other players read to me what was on the stops to the right and to the left before I could choose a direction to move.  

Lots of down time.  Since you don't know what others moves will be nor the roll of your die,you can't do much planning.  I just sat there waiting for my turn.

We played with 4, and often due to loss of multiple turns, it would be 6 to 9 opponent turns before I got another turn.  This happened to me over and over. That is just too much down time--can't imagine it with 6 players.

I can see playing this once a year.  Some of the expansions look good.

RATING: 10
Great old game with lots of fun memories.  Its a fun beer and pretzels outing for parents and kids or folks that don't normally game (and can enjoy a fantasy/storybook  theme).  It's a simple race game at heart to reach the center of the board.  You just roll a dice and read the instructions on the space you land in or on the cards you flip.   It's a breath of fresh air to play a game that's not a bunch of overlapping abstract mechanics that you have to groove your brain to 'get'.  It's just fun, creative storytelling with an RPG feel.  It's entertaining to see what happens to folks.  Fantasy Flight has done a great job with this game.  Enjoy the fantastic artwork and social aspects of playing this game!   
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 5
The most common complaint I read about Talisman I read is that it takes too long, too much randomness, too much just roll and move. And you know what, I would agree, though I would say the taking to long is a symptom rather than a problem itself. Because of the randomness of the encounter cards, players do not have much control over the growth of their character and because of this it takes much longer than it probably should to power up their characters enough to head towards the goal. At this point I don't think I'd choose this to play as a game. Instead I'd almost rather treat it like a toy of sorts, where I'm not really playing to try and win, but to wander around the board and see what happens to my character and at some point someone makes it to the middle of the board and it is time to put the toy away.

Expansions can mitigate some of the randomness issues, but sometimes I think that (adding too many new cards) the deck of Adventure cards may result unbalanced.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
I am a fan of both Talisman and Runebound, and in my opinion they are both flawed gems. 

I definitely miss Runebound's scalable encounters. It's nice to know that your level 1 character won't stumble upon Margath, for instance, unless you're silly enough to go right for a red challenge.

Compared to Runebound though, I actually prefer the movement mechanic of Talisman. Sure, most of the time your choice is limited to two directions (or a third if moving to or from the Plain of Peril). However, in Runebound, movement is the most AP prone element of the game.

The real winning factor for me is the dynamic nature of the Talisman board. The realm itself changes.

Talisman is not for everyone. It is an old school adventure game akin to Gygaxian "make a saving throw or your 12th level character dies" AD&D. It can be brutal at times. It is not kinder and gentler, and it usually won't help one's self esteem. 

Talisman is beer and pretzel, not wine and cheese.

Notes on the 4th edition:  Tarted up version of the 2nd edition.  Bigger board, plastic chits (though hard to read without modification), nice bits holder.  The cards are nice but the font is somewhat small.  The rules are slightly tweaked from 2e.  At long last a crafty character can turn in craft monsters to increase their craft.  That's been a house rule for a long time.  Also, the new rules provide useful options/suggestions to speed up play.  If you have 2e, it's probably not worth the purchase.  Still I like the bigger board and nicer components.

RATING: 3.5
Yup, the game is luck dependent, but this could have been fine. This is Talisman and not Chess. But for a fourth revised edition there are too many imbalances or evidently underdeveloped mechanics. Some characters are insanely overpowered while others are loosers. (Cultist, Assassin, Prophetess, Bounty Hunter on one side - Ghoul, Monk or sucker of suckers Priest on the other side)

Some items are a must have - Spell Book. There is so much pressure to have it, the game with City expansion should be renamed to "Spell Book" and the player to hold it for five turns should automatically win. BTW winning conditions are terrible. Dull, dull, dull, so very dull. Throw a die - nothing happened. Throw a die - 1 HP lost. Throw a die - nothing happened. Another OP item - heavy armour from the city in combination with Bounty Hunter = almost invincible character in combat. There are more thing like this - for instance all normal pieces of armour are rubbish. If you lose a fight they will steal your best item anyway.

Theme does not shine either. Imagine a hero (a troll for instance) with a horde of wierd fellows - mercenary, walking cabinet, gremlin, magic elephant, really small dragon, pixie, unicorn, gnome, old hag selling carrots, horse, a rather large herd of mules and a virgin. BTW, they are all flying a magic carpet.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
When I found out this edition was being released, I quickly unloaded my two complete sets of the second edition on eBay for a hefty sum.
This version cleans ups some ambiguities, and adds plastic minis, which is always better than those cardboard stand-ups.

One that has made it's way back into my collection, and was sorely missed the entire time we went without it.

Currently the kids' #1 choice for adventure games. Somehow this old title really nailed it, and I feel it hasn't been done better or more effectively than Talisman. Simple mechanics, which have been cleaned up in this edition, with a bit more control over the dice rolls has made this game the absolute best at portraying the classic fantasy adventure (although some ambiguities in wording still made their way into the rulebook). It's by far the most random, and non-forgiving fantasy adventure game out there. But that's the reason I like it, and it's an excellent introduction to the world of gaming for non-gamers.

Expansions are pretty much a must with this title. The vanilla game will get tired after a few plays, and adding extra cards for variety will keep the game exciting. With the two small box expansions (Reaper, and Frostmarch) alone, the sheer number of cards these two little boxes add to the game will keep it fresh for years. The rest are just icing on the cake.
 
A must-have for any adventure game fan.

Just completed the collection with the final few expansions I was missing. This feels like the Grail version of Talisman if there ever was going to be one. It will be tough to top in both amount of expansions, and excellent designed components. Unless the next edition has some amazing differences and improvements, I don't see there being another Talisman better than this version.

So long FFG, and thanks for all the Talisman.

RATING: 8
This was my gateway game. Very heavy on theme, but it is executed very well. Wonderful components and artwork. The game is criticized for its randomness and lack of strategy, but experienced players can leverage the randomness in their favor. The randomness is also part of the fun in my eyes. Tons of incredible characters with unique abilities. Each game is like a unique quest all its own. Great as a relaxed, fantasy adventure with some friends, though it can get intense as you race towards the crown of command. Several excellent expansions breathe new life into the game by adding new mechanics and characters.

Great fantasy game. Can be a little cumbersome for new players, but is totally teachable. Randomness can be leveraged based on strategies, but is largely luck of the draw/dice roll. If you're open to going on a fantasy adventure filled with random encounters around every corner, it's a great game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
I've owned or played most prior editions of this game and I think this FFG version is the best to date. The game looks great, particularly with painted figures. Even the dice are cool. The fate mechanic puts guardrails around some of the game's wilder swings of fortune, proving especially useful when threatened with a toading, or if the Reaper (from the expansion) comes calling. Adding a bonus strength or craft at the beginning speeds things up, and often it's worth calling the game when the first player gets to the Crown of Command, so the game doesn't drag on so terribly as used to be the case. I wouldn't play it with more than three, and I wouldn't play it with my "sophisticated" game night pals, but my nine-year-old thinks this is the coolest game in the world, and when I'm playing with him, I'm inclined to agree.

RATING: 10
The monopoly of RPGs, it is a must for every gamer. Very easy for everyone (kids, wife, etc) and they will love it from the first roll of the dice. Some says that it is totally random, but it is not! In every turn you have to take decisions like “is my craft enough to go deeper or should I take more experience by killing more monsters?”, “should I stay on this side of the board or should I go somewhere else with different cards dropped on the board” (when you draw cards sometimes they stay down like items, monsters, markets, etc... and the game board each time is different), “should I sacrifice my follower?”, “should I use one fate to reroll or to save it for future use?”, “should I use this spell now?”, “should I buy a sword or a helmet?”, “should I risk to attack the dragon to gain some strength faster or it is better to kill weaker enemies and grow slower”, “should I...”, “should I...”, “should I...”...Yes, you should... buy it and you will thank me for years of playing! Definitely 10...

Thanks to all the guys who said that it is a very good game and make me go and take it.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
If you want something light on rules but which has an epic feel, this is it. The "roll and move" is an ingenious mechanic to simulate an adventure. In an adventure, the journey between two points is never in a straight line. No destination can be reached without unexpected encounters along the way. The obstacles on your path can be brutal. But this game is also a race, so you need to raise your chin, push your luck, and deal with what happens.

Talisman is an excellent antidote to that disease of mind in which people become overly fixated on control in games. Like any adventurer, you need strength of will and hope more than you need certitude of calculation and planning. There are choices to be made in the game to be sure, but they are like choice you face at a crossroads. Which path will you take? Will you play it safe or take a risk?

Talisman games are fast paced and simple, but they feel epic. They are unpredictable, colourful, and they tell stories that are often filled with dramatic reversals (and reversals of reversals).

If you want to get the most of this game, add a layer of storytelling to it; don't just read the cards, weave a tale around them - a tale of evil or tragedy if you play an evil character, or a comedic tale of misshaps if the dice are against you!

RATING: 7
I can see the flaws with Talisman.  It's an old game (it must be - I remember wanting it when it was first released by GW), with roll and move mechanics that are way past their best-before date.  It can drag on forever.  It's random to a ludicrous degree.

The thing is, I really don't care. ;-)

Talisman, to me, is stupid, simple, unapologetic  fun. The fact that I can die on my very first turn with the unfortunate turn of a card and roll of a die? Hilarious. The fact that my oppoents can also be similarly squished? Even more hilarious.

A large part of this is, I'll admit, probably down to nostalgia.  That said, Talisman definitely scratches that dungon-crawling, loot-gathering itch quite nicely.

I recently finished painting all of the minis for the base game and The Reaper expansion and really most get some pics uploaded...

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
[center][size=6][COLOR=#878787]LIFETIME GAME [microbadge=28495]:star:[microbadge=28496] "PLAY FOREVER"[/COLOR][/size][/center]

[i][b]L[/b]ife is hard and the Gods are cruel; we toil for their amusement and even our best, most heroic efforts are but castles in the sand before the rushing tide. The Crown of Command dangles as a carrot on the end of a very beaty stick, existing only to see who will neck-stab whom for the illusion of control. We go now, doughty adventurers, hopping across this stage as toads to make the Gods—and perhaps ourselves—laugh. In the end, some lucky bastard will "win"—though he or she will most likely be consumed in capricious flames whence the curtain falls on this pointless shadow play.[/i]

[microbadge=2915]

This is NOT a nostalgia rating—I never got a chance to play this as a kid, teen, or college student.  Though I probably would have spent an awful lot of time doing so if I'd had the chance...

This is a GREAT nerd party/time-waster/beer, pretzels & potty-mouth game.  It has clumsy, outdated mechanics, "unfair" amounts of luck, and the ancient, tired and beaten-to-death [i]Lord of the Rings/D&D[/i] rip-off theme.

And I love it.

This is, in many ways, the Ultimate "Gone-Stupid" Game.  You can pull your brain out of gear and just coast along; it's one for those times when you would like to play a game, but life has hammered you down to the point where you just want to go "guh."

So roll a die, pull a card, read the result aaand...

ENJOY!

UPDATE:  Many people decry the random, binary movement system (roll a die and choose either right or left) but this simplicity is part of what makes [i]Talisman[/i] great—it's the only game of its ilk in which downtime is not an issue.  While [i]Runebound[/i] begins to drag at 3p (and becomes intolerable with any more), [i]Talisman[/i] can support the full compliment of players and the turns literally whiz around the table.  Roll, pick, do the thing, pass the dice.  It's almost a party game, it's so fast.

PS.  The new Fantasy Flight upgrade is fab!  Looking very forward to a whole mess of expansions...

UP-UPDATE:  With renewed family interest this has been hitting the table as a weekly event!  The good news, other than getting to play one of my favorite "weird storytelling" games, is that all the kids are hot to paint the scads of minis.  Several nights now I've gone to sleep only to wake to finished minis in the morning.  If you can engineer this effect for yourself I highly recommend it.

The only minor downer is that what makes this game fantastic is also the one thing that can kill it.  The utterly random element, so brilliant as a jumping-off point for spit-takes—like when the Leprechaun gets the Princess as a follower and ends up being lugged around in a front-facing baby carrier with a boob on each shoulder—can make the game excruciatingly slow when the cards don't come out in a useful manner.  After a couple of games of watching others level up ferociously while I got in multiple fights with a Royal Decree, three Horse Stables, several Bags of Gold, and a New Age strip-mall (the Mage, Healer and some dude hawking tie-dyed bedsheets decided to clog up the Hidden Valley), I've come to realize that more than anything else this game requires [i]stamina.[/i]
[floatright][imageid=1374144 small]
[size=7]Fig. 1 — [i]!!![/i][/size][/floatright]
With all the Adventure Cards from all the expansions, I'm thinking I might need to go through and trim the deck down to tighten up the game... though I'm conflicted, as [i]Talisman[/i] really is about embracing pure chaos and not every story should follow standard Fantasy tropes.  Sometimes it's okay if the Ogre Chieftain's saga is one of administration, finances and horse-trading.

[b]Recommended for Faster Play:[/b]

- Start the game with +1 Strength or Craft
- Gain Strength/Craft for every 5 points of trophies
- Remember that mechanically it's a push-your-luck race game without a timer—so push your luck and run that race as quickly as you can.  [b]Go for the inner region as soon as your Strength [i]or[/i] Craft is 9+.[/b]  On average this drives the game to a satisfying conclusion in about 90 minutes.*

[size=7]*Of course, True Fans see the lack of timer as a bonus, making [i]Talisman[/i] a fantasy bubble bath—complete with your favorite beverage and current love interest—to luxuriate in as you will.  Time means nothing if you love what this does.[/size]

RATING: 10
I swore to never post here again after the inexcusable banning of Mike Barnes, but, I decided I had to post a rating for this game to counter the low rating given by a certain prolific reviewer.  Talisman is and always will be a roll and move game with simple combat determined by a stat modified by a die roll.  Anything else and it ceases to be Talisman and there would be no point in a re-release.  If you got a new chess set you wouldn't give it low marks because "the components are nice but the fundamental rules of the game are the same".  Its chess.  It is what it is.  This is the same Talisman game that has been loved by gamers since 1983.  If you don't like it, fine.  But, don't rip on it for being what it is or being something it isn't.  It isn't Runebound.  It's Talisman and it is great, if you like Talisman.

There's a lot more strategy to this game than people give this game credit for--it's essentially a race game with everyone running along different shifting courses. 

If I'm in the mood to really fry my brain, Talisman kinda lingers sheepishly at the top of my closet--but if I'm in the mood for a rollicking unpredictable evening of light fantasy and dice-rolling, it jumps lovingly into my arms. Also--wife friendly (and I'm speaking of my wife in particular here--not at all claiming this is applicable to some undefinable set of "all wives")!

RATING: 7.5

Tips for success:

* Play quickly.

* Stop stressing out over things you can't control, which will be most things.

* Cheer for your opponents' successes. 

* Enjoy the ride.

2011-07-27

Initial Rating: 8.0 (May 2010)

LOVE the theme, Talisman was once in my top 10 and was one of the first games I played. In general, I don’t like games with a lot of luck, especially if they take a long time to play (as Talisman does) but I can make an exception here due to the great theme the game has, it also has tons of adventure cards so each play is different. The miniatures are very detailed and in general the components are great. On the bad side, the main mechanic is roll and move, also there are some characters that are really weak. 

So if you are looking for a game with deep strategic thinking go somewhere else, but if you are looking for a light random game (which takes a long time to play) here is Talisman. 

Current Rating: 6.5

RATING: 3
I bought this for nostalgia's sake as I loved the earlier version as a kid. I wish I hadn't gone back to it. The game is far far too random, the theme is fun typical high fantasy and not amazingly well done, the tweaks in the latest edition help mitigate randomness a little bit, but not enough. Not one intelligent decision to be made, this is a game requires you to just roll the dice, pick from two options, and roll again. Occasionally there is an obviously right decision, otherwise it is just a pointless dice fest. Serious runaway leader problems since you cannot do anything to the winning player unless the dice roll lets you catch them!

Good to keep yourself amused while watching an average movie and with some beers is about as good as it gets. 3 points for theme, art and components.

RATING: 7
I kick ass at this game--unfortunately, I have solved Talisman and it is no longer interesting to me.  The solution is as follows (spoiler alert!):

If your alignment is good, always move to the right.
If your alignment is bad, always move to the left.
If your alignment is neutral, alternate moves from right to left.

Neutral is the hardest to play as you have to remember, "Did I move right or left last time?"

But once you figure this out your friends might as well pack up and go home, cuz it's game over, y'all: COMMAND SPELL ZZZZZZAAAAAPPP!!!

In all honesty, my 7 rating is all about the escapism that Talisman offers.  And you better be damn sure to do everything in your power to escape, cuz I'm seriously gonna COMMAND SPELL your weak ass into oblivion. ZZZZAAAPPP!!!

RATING: 8
This is the first fancy board game i ever bought and it did not dissapoint me. The rules were easy to wrap your head around (at least for most of my friends) and it is really fun once you get used to focusing on your character(the items, stats etc.). That may take 2-3 games to get used to but it's all good. Sadly though the game is bound on luck  in most cases and, if a player gets lots of monsters and levels up well there is nothing you can do about it. He will probably steamroll you but it's all fine. One thing you want to do is encourage your friends to pvp. It adds a lot to the game. The characters are not in a rock paper scissor kind of relationship but sometimes you can't counter them. For example if you have low strength and you can't psychic combat the Troll will pwn you. The miniatures are beautifully sculpted. The art on the board and the cards are very nicely drawn.

RATING: 8
It´s simple and many people say it´s just a gateway-game for newbies. Well, it was indeed for me when I was young. But it is still one of the best fantasy-boardgames I ever played. It IS the simplicity and elegant game mechanism that makes me love it. The character management, well, it isn´t nearly as interesting as in WoW:BG and there is no such storyline like in Runebound - but it has cool character arche types, you can use items and magic spells, the game is fast paced... and there isn´t that much of downtime like in WoW or Runebound. Complexity is not always the best way. The game can be as long as WoW or Runebound (the endgame...) - but the player actions are done a LOT faster. Or said in other words: You play the same time as with WoW or RB, but you have done much more WITHIN this time... Well, if there wasn´t that much of randomness and luck... but that was the feeling of games in the 1980s :) I still like it very much for casual play.

RATING: 7
This was my gateway game. Very heavy on theme, but it is executed very well. Wonderful components and artwork. The game is criticized for its randomness and lack of strategy, but experienced players can leverage the randomness in their favor. The randomness is also part of the fun in my eyes. Tons of incredible characters with unique abilities. Each game is like a unique quest all its own.  Great as a relaxed, fantasy adventure with some friends, though it can get intense as you race towards the crown of command. Several excellent expansions breathe new life into the game by adding new mechanics and characters.

Great fantasy game. Can be a little cumbersome for new players, but is totally teachable. Randomness can be leveraged based on strategies, but is largely luck of the draw/dice roll. If you're open to going on a fantasy adventure filled with random encounters around every corner, it's a great game.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 6
Egyetlen félig lejátszott játék alapján a véleményem röviden: gyönyörű a tábla, de túl kevés a cselekvési lehetőség. Interakció van (amikor ugyanarra a mezőre lép két játékos, akkor harcolnak, meg - ki tudja? - talán spéci varázslatokkal vagy képességekkel vagy mezők hatásaival is lehet egymásra hatni, de túl kevés. A játék elég összetett, sok érték és tulajdonság van, sok varázslat, sok kártya, tárgyak, minden - ez így jól hangzik, de egyszerűen túl kevés a cselekvési lehetőség.

Amikor rám kerül a sor, dobok a kockával, és balra vagy jobbra (ezt én dönthetem el) annyit lépek, amennyit dobtam. Ez itt egy döntési lehetőség (mármint hogy merre menjek), és itt kb. vége is a sornak. Ahova megérkezem, ott vagy van már valamilyen lap a mezőn, pl. egy szörny, és akkor harcolok vele (dobókocka + módosító értékek), vagy húzok egy lapot, ami a következőként az adott mezőre érkező játékosra fog hatni (általában), vagy a mező speciális képességét hajtom végre (ami általában szintén kockadobás-alapú, pl.: 1-et dobsz: kimaradsz a következő körből; 6-ot dobsz: kapsz egy aranyat). Ez így elég kevés önálló, meghatározó döntés a játékos részéről (sőt, szinte semennyi), és ez a játék nagy hibája.

Megjegyzendő még, hogy a tábla kifejezetten nagy méretű, és rengeteg felirat olvasható rajta, amiket el is kell olvasni. Gyakran előfordul, hogy olyan szöveget kellene elolvasni, ami a tábla túlsó felén, apró betűkkel, fejjel lefelé található. Ilyenkor vagy oda kell menni hozzá (ehhez körüljárható asztal kell), vagy megkérni valamelyik ott ülő játékostársat, hogy olvassa fel a szöveget. Idővel persze fejből is megtanulja az ember, hogy melyik mezőre mi van írva, és azt is, hogy melyik mezőn lévő kártyalap mire szolgál, így nem kell olvasni, de ez messze nem az első játék alatt történik meg.

Amúgy szívesen végigjátszanám egyszer, mert kellemesen eltelik az idő a játék körül, de hiányoznak a döntési lehetőségek, és azok súlya, ezért nem lesz igazán jó ez a játék. Játszható, könnyen bele lehet jönni, mert a hosszú és összetett szabálykönyv valójában egyszerű mechanizmusokat és szabályokat tartalmaz, de nem egy év játéka.

RATING: 6.5
Si te gustan los juegos de rol, si jugaste al Hero Quest, si te apetece pintar figuras (y se te da bien), aquí tienes Talisman, un juego donde podrás elegir entre más de 10 personajes distintos (mago, enano, guerrero, troll, hechicera, sacerdote...) con sus respectivas figuras y particulares y específicas habilidades especiales para recorrer el peligroso mundo de Talisman (una versión fantástica del juego de la oca) en el que tendrás que usar tu fuerza y astucia, tu espada y tus conjuros para hacer frente a eventos adversos, feroces enemigos y maliciosos rivales que harán lo imposible para evitar que entres en el valle de fuego, te hagas con la corona de mando y elimines al resto de rivales, siempre y cuando no seas convertido mediante una maldición en un viscoso sapo.
Y es que Talisman te hará pasar muy buenos ratos en épicas partidas donde puede pasar cualquier cosa y cualquier jugador puede ganar, ya que es un juego de dados, y el azar, ya se sabe, es caprichoso; no es por tanto, un juego de grandes estrategias en el que estrujarse el cerebro, no es un juego de jugadores, sino un juego para todos los públicos, divertido, ameno, y que anima a seguir jugando probando todos los diferentes personajes de que dispone, lo que aumenta su rejugabilidad,potenciada tambien con las diversas (hasta el momento 4, aunque todas en inglés) expansiones del juego.

RATING: 7.5
Played with 6. The game is very random, one player WILL get screwed over, either by the cards or by the other players. If you learn this game, there is alot of downtime. It wasn't until everyone gave up trying to do strategies and just went with the flow a bit more, that gameplay started to get faster. Also, we didn't wait for one player to completely finish his turn, when the next one started rolling for his. At one point 4 players were doing their turns at the same time, result was a bit messy, but much more fun than waiting it out every turn. There isn't that much that you can do to mess it up that way, except with casting spells and landing on the same spot, and being ex-Magic players we just treated that all as a twisted form of "the stack". Works for us, made the game enjoyable. 

Would be a 6 if you wait the turns out, 7,5 as it is right now with the turns through one another and the fast play-speed.

RATING: 9
It is a random game, I give all the haters that, but when does "random" became automatically "boring" or dull. 

Yes, The Game of Life and Monopoly use dice,but the comparison stops there. Monopoly is a negotiation game at heart, I "like it", The Game of Life is totally about randomness without an apex of theme or any strategy, tactics or engaging elements whatsoever. Sure, games like Agricola are "manageable" and stragetic, and the choices are up to you all the time, and when you play it without the cards, the game is practically random-less,  but not only the mechanics or the strategy make a game fun, engaging and/or interesting. At least for me. 

Talisman does that exactly, it engages me in a quest where random events happen and where a bad roll will kill you, but the game is so easy, so light and so FUN in the clearest of terms that I REALLY DON'T CARE. The game is awesome and I look forward to play it lots and lots of times, the variety in the main box is awesome and even when the fixed board and the 14 heroes become old (even when that seems a great number, in a game where 1-2 players die each game, the number becomes small)  and the game  becomes a little bit repetitive after some plays, again I don't care, because I'm $15 from a huge variety (small expansion) or $30 away from a whole new world (large expansion). By the way that's why this is a 9 (if you were wondering) because the game need expansions and I don't mind buying them.

A definite new jewel that feeds to my AT needs.

RATING: 3
My disappointment with this game was staggering. I remember drooling over the ads for Talisman in Dragon magazine when I was a teenager, and if it wasn't for Games Workshop's (at that time, anyway, justifiably) exorbitant prices I would have snapped it up eagerly. It was so pretty, and looked so cool.

I cannot describe how happy I am now that I didn't. It's not far from being a Monopoly variant, only the downtime is worse and you don't even have the appeal of making money (well, a gold here and there, but that's it). All it has going for it, in comparison, is some extremely nice art, albeit in a style I'm no longer drawn to, and the ability to choose which direction you want to go. Otherwise, it is a bog-standard roll-and-move game with a rather dull combat system pasted on. It is entirely possible to be dropped in an enormous hole by the dice, at which point you need a huge stroke of luck to rescue you from getting the crap beat out of you by the luckier players. It doesn't even finish any faster than Monopoly.

Maybe the biggest disappointment of my boardgaming life.

RATING: 8
Like the new set.  Production value of the art is high, but I still like the Wayne England art in 3rd edition a bit better--the art on the new main board outer region could have had a lot more character to it (see the new dungeon board for a good example of what they should have gone for). They have some good new rules (Spells) and surprisingly allowed you to turn in craft monsters for XP(!?). Picked up the FF Reaper, Upgrade kit and Dungeon and it's cooking with gas so far.  A few very strange decisions (monk, warhorse, raiders nerfs) but other than that FF has this back on track.

RATING: 7.5
[microbadge=419][microbadge=670]

For a roll-and-move game of square blobs, Talisman certainly makes you feel like you're in a fully developed fantasy world.  Maybe it's because the tropes are so familiar, but still so appropriately rendered.  Luck is a cruel mistress in this game, especially when trying to enter the next circle, but that is largely mitigated by the incredibly fast turns.  Combat is a breeze as well.  Really, only spell-casting can slow the game down.  The larger number of characters is cool, offering plenty of strategy in games to come.  Good and solid fantasy board-gaming.

RATING: 8
I don't think I've ever played a game the enjoyment of which depends so much upon upon its players' states of mind. 'Cause, yeah, the common complaints on the Geek about TALISMAN are right on the nose - it takes way too long for even a fairly devoted set of gamers, and the roll & move mechanic can easily become almost grindingly tedious. But if you're playing with a group of people who have all prepared themselves to look past this stuff, then the gorgeous and cleverly differentiated ways in which each character gradually gains strength and resources, and the subtle shift in stakes as they start to enter the inner circles of the board, can make for a totally absorbing and suspenseful four-hour session. 

Plus, the components really are beautiful. People have said a lot about the figures on here, but what really stands out for me is the card art, which is always worth taking a second look at and can really be useful in establishing mood.

RATING: 5
An old game updated by Fantasy Flight where you start on an outer ring and roll and move.  You get a card which can be a monster, treasure or an event depending on the space.  Once you have increased your abilities, you can move to a second smaller ring.  You keep rolling and moving until you make it to the inner ring.  Once there you can attack all other players, where they can lose a life.  If all other players are eliminated, you win.  

Long, tedious and boring.  But, it can be fun if you know what you are getting into and understand that it is based on luck and is pretty light. A good game to play with friends who don't really want to do anything heavy.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.4
This is a game that has steadily grown on me over the years.  I wasn't one of those people that grew up with the game, I only recently discovered it around 2010, but even without the nostalgia factor, I've grown to love it.  A lot of people misjudge the game as a simplistic "fantasy monopoly" where there is zero strategy or depth.  This couldn't be any further from the truth.  The game is deceptively deep and engaging if you take the time to understand it.

Unlike Runebound, the world of Talisman becomes more and more interesting with time because monsters, treasure and events begin to populate the world.  Expansions just add to the experience.  Every time I play, I feel like I'm going on a real adventure in an awesomely beautiful fantasy world (best card art of any game I own), with lots of freedom and multiple goals to undertake.

I could go on and on, but suffice it to say, Talisman is a gem that delivers an fantasy epic story with simple mechanics in a reasonable amount of time that works for your whole family.

Must have expansions are: The Reaper, The Dungeon and The City.  I also own The Highland, The Woodland, The Sacred Pool, The Harbringer, and Cataclysm.

RATING: N/A
Talisman is a cult classic board game with a fantasy theme. There are 14 characters a player can control, from the heroic Warrior to the powerful Sorcerer. In this perilous adventure, play centers around the journey of these gallant heroes to find and claim the Crown of Command, a magical artifact with the power to destroy all rivals and make the bearer the true ruler of the kingdom. Only with strength, courage, wisdom and a few good dice rolls will players be able to survive the ultimate test and beat their opponents to victory.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
The Cataclysm expansion is a must-have 

House rules:
1) leveling up requires one more points of Strength/Craft trophies than your current Craft/Strength, but never more than 7,
2) If you only have one Talisman in your possession, it cannot be taken/stolen by another  character.

3) If a character dies mid-game, the replacement character inherits all his Craft/Strength points, and one Talisman of his choice, (if the previous  character had one in his possession ). 

4) Every character starts the game with a random Warlock Quest card.

I had a good time playing. We'll see how it ages; I liked Runebound at first, but my opinion of that game has slowly declined over the last couple years.

RATING: 7
Holy shit, this game is too long. Our first game was four hours, and the first three were great. Not knowing what to expect from the middle and inner rings, we mostly dorked around on the outer ring, learning the ropes; tons of fun, except for the one player who got screwed for 75% of that time by bad die rolls.

Once we hit the middle ring in earnest, the last hour was pure pain and boredom. The player who made it to the crown didn't have fun, because his turn was reduced to one 50/50 die rolls, and randomness soured almost everything at that point. I spent many, many turns not rolling what I needed to hit the damned portal.

75% fun + 25% I never want to play this again = I see the fast-play rules in our future if this one hits the table again.

After a second game, that's more like 40% fun + 60% hell. It's roll and move, swingy, and while it's fun for the first hour the remaining 1-2 hours can be really awful. I'd much rather sit down for a long game like Battlestar that's consistently fun -- and even fun to lose, which Talisman is not.

---

Between my second and third play, I revised my attitude towards Talisman and resolved to take it on its own terms: grab an adult beverage, expect a beer and pretzels game, laugh at your buddies (and yourself), and don't worry about winning. If by some chance I acquired enough stuff to go for the crown, I would; if not, I'd have fun doing whatever happened -- picking the thing that sounded most entertaining and just rolling with it.

And it worked! This turned Talisman into an enjoyable game for me. So much so that I re-rated it from a 3 to a 7. It's outside my wheelhouse in a lot of ways, and I don't think it'll ever be a go-to game, but taken as more of a fun ride than a game to devote much brainpower to, it's actually quite fun.

RATING: 9
I. love. euro-games. Why then can't I play this game enough? What hold do you have over me Talisman? What dark secrets lend you your power?

In all seriousness, this game should not exist, and is basically mocking modern game design. Un-balanced starting players. A completely random, from super good cards, to completely deadly monsters in the adventure deck. Player elimination. ROLL AND MOVE. Super, super long, and it doesn't really scale well in terms of game length. More players increases the time length linearly. And yet it all works. To the game's credit, there are some fancy, behind-the-scenes game mechanics to keep it flowing smoothly, and make it fun. But at the end of the day, Talisman is just the Ameritrash-iest Ameritrash, and I can't play it enough. Bravo Talisman, bravo.

RATING: 1

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
This game is a classic.  Very easy to learn, and fun to play.  Similar mechanic to Monopoly, as in a player rolls a die, and moves that many spaces.  The player either lands on a good space, or a bad space.

An average game will last about 2 hours, depending on how many players are playing.  There are a lot of cards to collect, such as items, and allies.  The game is very random, as it involves rolling dice to move (and just about everything else), and drawing of many, many random cards.

There are 14 characters to chose from, each with special abilities, which offer a nice variety.  In a sense, this game is like an RPG (role playing game), much like Descent: Journeys into the Dark.  Unlike Descent, Dungeon & Dragons, etc., you do not need an Overlord \ Dungeon Master to play.  This game can be played by two players, whom both control a hero each.  This makes Talisman a great 2 player game.

There are many items to collect, many monsters to slay, and many interesting places to see.  Due to it's randomness, each game session is very unpredictable.  

Each player tries to level up their character, and collect as many powerful items as possible, so that they can undertake the main challenge, and win the game.  While the game is designed to be competitive, it can also be played co-operatively, although, it probably won't be as fun.

While for the most part, most people will agree that Runebound 2nd ed. by Fantasy Flight Games, is better, and more complex, it does not take any fun away from Talisman.  Talisman allows players to interact with each other more so than Runebound.  A Runebound game also has the tendency to drag on, and last longer than it should.

With Fantasy Flight Games taking over Talisman, the game should only get better from this point on.  There will be new models released for all the characters, and new interesting expansions!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 4
It's a push your luck and stab your buddies dice rolling game. I played it twice just to make sure of my impression, as the first group I played it with was risk averse and had no interest in winning, they just wanted to have all the best cards. There isn't much more skill in this game than Sorry!

For those who say it is like D&D, I wonder who the heck they were playing with. Yes, Gygax was involved in both, but these are totally different games. D&D is about working together to accomplish your goals, Talisman is a solitaire drag, where player interaction only occurs by chance (with a little choice), and only in an exploitative way. This describes the game in a nutshell: roll dice, flip cards, roll dice, pass dice, wait for everyone else to do the same, rinse, repeat. D&D should involve making decisions with the input of others, not just rolling dice all day with very little need of player interaction.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
'It plays like a story written by a six year old boy forced to churn out a four hundred page fantasy novel.'
- One of The Haters

'That's what makes it awesome.'
-One of the fans.

The ultimate edition of the ever popular Talisman, its family-friendly nature and no-brainer gameplay continue to earn its cult reputation into the 21st century.

Talisman is essentially a non-gamers' fantasy adventure game. Its NOT really strategic (although you will learn tricks for success), it IS chaotic as heck and CAN go on for literally hours, but there's plenty of daft fun and entertainment to be had if you take it the right way! 

Its clichéd fantasy theme cocktail and lasting variety makes up for its lame roll-and-move-and-roll gameplay. Its best used as a gamers party game- get some drinks and munch in, have a laugh and don't take it too seriously!

Its not the winning, but the long and chaotic journey that counts. Its about laughing when all your stuff is nicked by raiders and then you run into a Dragon (Strength 7). What happens then? Well you go to the tavern and get blind drunk in the corner, that's what!

The revised 4th edition is like the final draft, with beautiful board art, pimped up components (little talisman gold coins anyone?!), more balanced cards and characters and a swath of expansions to keep it from getting too old. The addition of Fate also adds a huge element of strategy. The only complaint I can really level at it is that the enhanced artwork makes the game feel a little too dry and serious for what it is.

Just remember not to bloat Talisman with too many expansions at once- the large box ones in particular will over complicate what was never meant to be a complicated game!

Lastly note that this game will NOT appeal to gamers who cannot immerse themselves into the theme of board games. Playing this game from a purely straight robotic point of view will feel lifeless and boring.

My friends still joke often about old games of Talisman  and I'm sure they will continue to do so for many years to come. Its not just a board game, its a magical quest adventure game, and its a good bit of fun from time to time.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

Not by any means the best game that I own, but it is the one I love the most. The atmosphere is fantastic. I have all expansions and together they create a massively epic experience.

RATING: 8
Adventuring light RPGstyle game; endgame is to become strong enough to overcome trials via stat checks etc.  4th ed seems more polished than the 2nd/3rd ed, adds fate counters (allows reroll) and has a lot of expansions.  Has PVP though no elimination; being killed you make a new character.  Good scope for personalisation/customisation/house rules.

RATING: 3
The multiple reprints and editions shouldn't fool you: Talisman is little more than a memento from an era when fantasy Candy Land was enough to find itself an unchallenged spot in the market. The ability to choose between going left or right is not really enough to keep me engaged; then the roll-and-move, random event cards and swingy characters/items basically feel like playing an RPG session run by a 5 year old GM with anger management issues. Some people might find it so random it's funny and perhaps this is intended as a lazy Sunday afternoon family game; but the swingy nature of the beast can make it quite unbearable for kids because higher player counts might cause a single game to last 3+ hours.

I haven't played any expansion, but it's worth noting that if you're not from the US, you might want to buy a bigger table before considering them.

RATING: 5
If we're going to play an RPG-adventure game, I will pull this out. I've tried Runebound, Prophecy, and others and each of those games try (without succeeding, IMO) to bring strategy to what is already a chromed-out luckfest. 

Talisman keeps things simple. Roll the die, kill some stuff. There is some light strategy--when to move inward, when to attack other characters, where to go with which character--but by and large it's simple. Ideally, the players are almost playing simultaneously. We can fit a 4p game in 60 minutes. Also, it's so simple to teach to new players!

It's not a serious game (nor are any of the other more complex alternatives going to create an RPG experience without a DM and hours of time), but played with this mindset, I have a lot more fun. I have cried of laughter several times.

Mage Knight and Magic Realm are very well the nadir of RPG-adventure gaming, but I just don't have the time or mental energy to commit to them.
