RATING: 8
I will admit a big portion of this high ranking is because of the many hours and days of fun I had with this game some 20 years ago. The new 4th edition is definitely an improvement mechanically, FFG have really improved the game. The game has features which many people hate - lots of randomness, possibility to lose everything you worked for, takes too long to play, and all sorts of other crazy stuff which is largely outside the player's control. However, I love it as anyone can win and be competitive. It's brutally cut-throat and confrontational, most of the luck can be mitigated, the game itself beats you up if you take too many risks, and you never really know what's going to happen next. Great for an epic adventure game with many twists and turns.

RATING: 5
I played talisman as a kid and remember it much differently than I do now.

The game is definitely an entry level fantasy board game.  It leaves a TON to be desired and the balancing is pretty garbage.  Sometimes spells feel powerful, but most of the time you're sitting with a max spell hand and have no beneficial use for them.

I only come out of a bored daze when facing players who are super adversarial, but they can't really get much done if they don't roll the right number.  I've had two players just flipping back and forth around me because they were one or two numbers to high.  These sort of dice movement adventure games make no sense.

It's decent and pretty much anyone can play, but after a few runs you're good for a few years I think.

RATING: 7
Beautiful game and excellent components! When we are in the mood to play Talisman we have a blast playing. The roll and move can get annoying for my wife. If there was some way to get around the need to roll an exact number to land on a spot...a variant or something...I know she would play this all the time. 

That being said however, this game is really awesome! The fun of roaming the board having any and all kinds of adventurers and the many many different characters you can choose to play make this game so much fun! The game is funny, (i.e. being turned into a toad for a few turns after an adventure turned bad). The character alignment is also a great feature (you can be good, evil or neutral).

The fact that all players are in a race to become strong enough to make the journey to the Crown of Command, takes this game to a whole new level. And then, once someone gets to the crown, everyone else on the board is hit with the Command spell that zaps the life out of them. If two or more characters find themselves at the Crown...they must battle to the death. Last man standing wins! The whole concept is pure genius and so much fun to play.

RATING: 9
  I like heavy eurogames. I like games which offer me many different strategies (Caylus being one of my favorites). So why the hell did I rate this game so high? 
   For almost 3 years I hunted for modern adventure board game to replace Talisman (2 ed.). There were great number of them, but none survived the test of time. Games like Runebound or Return of the Heroes seemed to promise more freedom to player and more choises. I was wrong. Sure, there were some interesting choises, but their core they were very random and had many flaws. Runebound had serious downtime problem, lack of interraction among players and very boring gameplay (kill - buy stuff - reperat 10 times or more). Return of the hereos in spite of nice flavour started to be repetitive very soon (every game I played had almost the same quests). Dungeoneer happened to be dependent on luck with card drawing. Only Prophecy seems to have really good mix of flavour, balance and strategic choises - but at cost of very long and tedious gameplay thanks to much to slow character progress. Maybe it is possible to reduce the time up to 1,5 hour? We`ll see. 
  So, the wheel of time circled to the starting point. Then I found Talisman 4th edition. Its graphic desing immidiately reminded me old favorite paintings by Larry Elmore from classic D&D rulebooks (mid 80`). I finely realised that adventere board game I want to play doesn`t need to be about a strategy but rather a flavour. This game should have little downtime, possible players interraction and offer suprises. It doesn`t need to be fair. It doesn`t need to be very strategic. But you should never be sure what is it going to happen. 
  And so it is Talisman 4th edition. I hate games which promise to be strategic but in fact are luck dependent. This game doesn`t promise that and never did. If you are looking for some serious strategy - this game disappoints you, i`m sure. But if you leave your adult disilusionment behind the door and open yourself for the sense of adventure you will probably find it. I found my board game adventure here, in the land of Talisman.

Edit: I lower my rate to 9. I did it because of lack of opportunity to play it as often as I would. But it`s still one of my favourites.

Edit: My eldest son became a fan so I gave his my copy :)

RATING: 10
Love this game.

I'm a competitive person. So I have to remind myself to not play Talisman competitively if I want to enjoy myself. It took me a a bit to come to terms that Talisman is more aptly thought of as social gaming. 

Play on 4th ed. is slightly different than 3rd ed.  Once you get to the Crown of Command, you are basically trying to take out all opponents through attrition rolls. And they're trying to get there also to eliminate you before that happens.  

In more then a few games, because of this, it has come down to the absolute wire. Which always is a great time!

*After probably 25-30 games, I have finally had the famous "game of Talisman that would just not end". I was well suited and prepped and shot into the Crown of Command. I should have been taking people out fairly quickly, but DAMMIT! A healer showed up in middle circle and a Mike had the Poltergeist. This enabled him to move one space- ramp up by killing a monster- I'd maybe cause one or two hits on him and he'd move right back to the healer using the poltergeist (one step per move). FINALLY he and the others ramped up their characters, came in the inner circle & I proceeded to finish them off. I hope something like that never happens again. We played with the Reaper- but the Reaper really didn't have much impact on play.

*If not playing with just 2-3 players, you'd best play "Sudden Death", where first person to get to Crown instantly wins. Also, start with extra strength or Magic and ramp up at 6 vs. 10. Even with that, a 5P game can be extremely long.

*******MY PREFERRED WAY OF PLAYING***************

I now like playing these variants to speed it up-

-Roll 2x D6 and choose one of them as your movement die (outer realm only).
-Start with extra life AND craft.
-Ramp up at 5 (or 4 even) points of strength and craft.
-Sudden death- first in to center wins.

Doing this usually makes games come in ~2hours

*Reaper expansion is now permanently mixed in. 

*Dungeon, Dragon, Blood Moon, Sacred Pool and Frostmarch expansions all contained in Dragon expansion box. Also have Harbinger and Cataclysm expansions in own boxes.

RATING: 9.25
Very fun fantasy adventure game with admittedly a lot of luck, but it's not totally devoid of strategy. Additional expansions tend to add more ways to get stronger and enter the Inner Region. The base game arguably has a greater luck factor than it does when expansions are included (particularly the board expansions). I feel like I can get really involved in my character in this game. The art is usually beautiful and the components are generally well crafted (although some of the miniatures look a tad wonky on occasion). This game is a behemoth in terms of playing space, though, especially so with extra expansion boards, so make sure you have a big table or at least a comfortable floor. All in all, I will always be willing to play a game of Talisman. Just know that I can be pretty merciless.

I play with the Reaper, Frostmarch, Sacred Pool, Dungeon, Highland, and City expansions, and I'm going to own the Nether Realm expansion soon. I played with the Dragon expansion, but I wasn't a fan of that because it added a lot of tedium to the game for very little added gameplay.

RATING: 9
A terrific adventuring game.

Doesn't provide many decisions during play (roll, move, read the board space and/or cards and follow the instructions). There is also a lot of luck involved and probably not a whole lot of skill. It can be a lengthy game, especially with many players.

Components (Revised 4th Edition) are great, although I don't particularly care for minis in general as I'd rather not have to paint them to distinguish between all the grey figures on the board. RATING: 9
I’m a bit of a trashy gamer which is why Talisman is one of my favorites, despite its many problems. Very few games are able create an emergent story in the same way Talisman can. While unbalanced, I enjoy the large amount of playable characters since it makes every game feel different, even though you’re doing mostly the same things. Its heavy use of dice based mechanics comes off as dated as hell, although I don’t mind it, since I’m fine with playing around probabilities rather than absolutes (rolling to move is the exception here, and while there are ways to make it easier to get the number you want, it’s needlessly frustrating). I enjoy how the board is built up as the game moves forward, and the initial simplicity of the game and its mechanics makes it easy for non-gamers to understand before things get trickier late game. 

Although I really like this game, I have a lot of reservations as well. The game goes on for far too long, which isn’t a problem in and of itself, although the lack of complex mechanics can make it boring (corner board expansions go a long way to mitigate this, and I don’t recommend playing without The Dungeon at least). The characters are wildly unbalanced even in the base game, and I ended up removing half from the deck since my group consistently neglects them. Down time can be quite long with groups of 4 or more players, especially in the late game when players are developing more robust strategies to win.

Despite its many flaws, I keep coming back to Talisman since it offers a very specific, simplistic, and old-school style of fantasy adventure. Newer adventure games don’t really scratch that same itch for me. Definitely not for everyone, however.

(I definitely did not write all of this to justify giving this game a 9 haha what)

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
My experience with Talisman has been long and varied.  I got into the second edition back in the 80s.  Loved it, played it to death.  After hundreds of games I lost interest in the game for about a decade. 

Lo and behold, here comes the FFG version.  I had to give it a try if only for old times sake.  After on play I realized how much I missed Talisman.  It's such a great game and the FFG version is the best Talisman ever even without the expansions.

Talisman gets a lot of grief for being a roll and move game.  And on your turn that is basically what you do.  You roll the die and then have an encounter on the space you land on.  Encounters either hurt your or give you various kinds of upgrades.  Once a player is strong enough and has a Talisman they can attempt to cause the game end condition by moving through the "inner region" to the Crown of Command space.  The Crown of Command allows you to kill off the other players.  Last person standing wins.

My favorite things about Talisman are the die rolling, the variety of adventure and character cards.  Why is dice rolling so awesome in Talisman?  First of all it makes down time virtually nil.  You roll the die, move, have an encounter, next person's turn.  But there's more thematic reasons for the die roll.  Let's say you were in the city and wanted (or needed) to go to the Tavern.  If you roll a six for movement you can move straight to it.  Frankly, there are not a lot of individual spaces on the Talisman board and too much determinism would make the game linear and boring.  But because you have to roll the die the likely hood is that you will have to land on a few non-Tavern spaces prior to getting to the Tavern.  And these non-Tavern spaces will likely require yout to draw one of a vast number of adventure cards.  The adventure deck contains all sorts of things from powerful enemies to useful items to board-wide events.

Sure your journey from the City to the Tavern could be quick and uneventful, but that would make for a pretty boring adventure.  Instead the die rolls and Adventure cards provide many a twist and turn.

Additionally anyone interested in Talisman should read this article by Aarontu:
http://boardgamegeek.com/thread/438714

I've got the up-grade pack! WOOT! "I'm a real game now!"

RATING: 7
A very easy, highly luck-based questing game with a vast array of character choices and a large number of different encounters. This game hit it off very well with a group of non-gamers, but its biggest downfall is a ridiculous game length. 

Even with the "rules for faster gameplay", it can take several hours to complete the game (depending on the number of players). Many games I've played have had to be ended prematurely by just declaring a winner because they were dragging on far too long. I certainly don't mind playing a long game, but only if its a game with meaningful strategic choices to be made throughout. 

As I explain to everyone when I teach them this game, "It's mostly a game where you just roll the die and see what happens."

RATING: 5
Please, know this game before you try to play it or teach it.  Recognize when a player has a combination of cards like a curse that will never let them do something fruitful before an hour or two goes by. Please, know who your opponents are so you can use the large amounts of downtime fruitfully to catch up, instead of dropping this four hour brick on two to four people who never played, and one who knew how to play it better than you, and nearly all of them strangers to you.  Please buy the excellent app and let it manage the game rules you do not know against A.I. opponents.

it's not an awful game if you play it with the right people, but it is a long slog of a game where you must eliminate all other players.  Make sure everyone knows it, make sure they are okay with that.  Grind your character into dominant positions by maximizing its stats.

UPDATE okay maybe some nostalgia was involved, its not the second edition Gary Chalk, which for me is  part of that the appeal of that edition. but its looks great.
The gameplay is good but the ending needs to be a bit more dynamic than just reach the x spot.

RATING: 8.5
Very nice, immersing game.
Easy to play and easy to teach to newbies.
Enough randomness to avoid "chess mentality" calculation.
But, when one has played it a number of times, there are strategical and tactical choices that usually make the difference between winning and losing the game.
In addition, as expressed in the first line, one is really led to feel that he is living an adventure - without all the organizational clutter of an RPG.
There is player interaction too: a lot of fun jumping upon an opponent to steal his talisman (if you are a thief) or rip it from him (by means of direct combat).
All in all, a pleasing, easy and fun game.

RATING: 4

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
If you like a (heroic) fantasy setting then Talisman will not disappoint. The strength of Talisman is its (very nice looking) board with all its possibilities that change with time. Many of the adventure cards are also 'Place (location)' cards that stay at specific locations generating a new board within the board (excellent drawing in the cards by the way). I believe that's the reason that the game creator(s) made a large board. You certainly need a big table to play the game and even larger if you plan to use one of the big expansions.

I also do not share some criticisms from other players concerning too much randomness in Talisman. For instance after a dice rolling for motion you have the choice to either go left or right on the board, therefore mitigating the consequences of a bad roll.
Furthermore, the 'fate' tokens can be useful in this regard and can help the characters devise a strategy in their explorations towards specific locations in the board.

 Expansions also look promising to create a more immersive atmosphere. Not a perfect game by all means but it does its job.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5.8
This isn't really a game so much as an activity. 
Pros
This is a fun and entertaining activity, if not much of a game. The board is beautiful and I've painted the figures quite nicely.

Cons
The only choices that the players make are whether to move clockwise or counterclockwise and when to move between the regions of the board. Everything else is determine by a dice roll. Having so much determined by luck isn't necessarily a bad thing so long as there is also an element of strategy that is under the control of the players. In Talisman, however, the players are only along for the ride. Now, if someone figures out how to add some euro elements to the game that would be very interesting indeed. 

Addendum: We've started adding house rules to reduce the luck slightly and speed up the game; e.g., we allow players a choice for movement: stay put, move one space or roll the die.

RATING: 9
Nostalgia makes this game shine for me.  It is a playable D&D stand-in (playable in the sense that adults with responsibilities, families, jobs, etc. can get together with a few friends and knock off a session of Talisman in a few hours).  Beautiful artwork, design one has come to expect from fantasy stalwart FFG, and thoughtful tweaks to the overall design make improvements to an otherwise imperfect yet enjoyable dungeon crawler.

I understand the "it's just roll & move" complaint--I do--I just disagree.  It ain't chess.  It's a theme showcase, and oozes with atmosphere.  I sometimes wish there was a bit more to the primary mechanic than 1D6, but yet still always want to play and always enjoy myself--even if ribbitting around the board for a few turns.

The Fate tokens are an interesting addition--but (as has often been the case with FFG games) they put 98% of the design skill into the game itself, and 2% into storing this monster.  High-quality bits, artwork, and overall quality still shine, though; with the anticipated several expansions this will become a game that does not travel well and will become more and more "stores in one box" prohibitive.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 10
No, there isn't much game there. But after so many very complex fantasy games, there's a sense of clear-headed enjoyment to just rolling and moving. Talisman is the sort of game that everyone should play when they are young, before we become too old to just have fun. The lack of control results in an adventure game that actually feels adventurous.

The game can take a little long, but I like that you have to decide when you want to try to win. It forces you to go for the kill, and a lot of games are satisfied to just let you go through the motions. That sense of proactive-ness is one thing I love about Talisman.

*edit* After four games of this, I kind of love Talisman. I'm bumping up my rating to a 10, simply because the prospect of getting to play genuinely excites me. I finished a two-hour game last night with three expansions, and I already want to go again.

RATING: 6
Ranked high for nostalgia reasons, so YMMV. W/O nostalgia, it would be a 5 for me. 

My houserules (of course! it's Talisman!): 

1. always allow a character to choose between moving 1 (walking), and rolling the die (taking a caravan). 

2. always allow a character to spend gold to add to movement, 1 for 1. 

3. Stat scores max out at 12 (followers, objects can raise stats above 12 while held).

4. Five stat worth of defeated creatures traded in for a Character stat point (not Seven, as in RAW)

5. Talismans can be spent as fate.

6. dice can 'critical hit' - meaning that for characters and creatures, a roll of 6 in combat means roll again and add it to the total (ad infinitum)

7. If you lose a gold but don't have any, lose a life instead.

8. you can quest for a stat, a gold, or to change alignment, as well as for a talisman. You must complete a quest to begin another.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7
Nice dice and coins in this edition, slightly pointlessly bigger board (the inner region is especially a waste of space - the obvious place to dump your adventure card stack, suspiciously large enough to fit a whole extra board...).

I much prefer the old Gary Chalk and John Blanche art, but the new stuff is nicely done (notably inferior to Runebound artwork).

Nothing done to address the old balance issues to prevent the game becoming 'Gnomequest'. Only innovation being allowed to collect Craft points -  which now creates a new balance issue of craft being too easy to boost.

FFG's tweaks seem to be a bit more thought through, and now there is a hope of decent expansions, maybe some life will be breathed into this fondly remembered game.

RATING: 5
Overall, I'm never influenced much by the way a game looks, so all the glitz won't gain any points with me. I find this edition of an old standby over 20 years to be perfectly playable. But (without a labored list of details), its mechanics lean a little more random than in the 2nd edition, which I still consider to be superior. I'm also one who doesn't care how long a game takes so long as the journey along the way is great. Endings don't matter much compared to that, and the push in the current edition toward making the game play faster and faster isn't a plus to me. In fact it is pushed so hard that some routes for winning are more and more shortcutting the need to find the games namesake and core fixture... a Talisman.  So my rating is basically that the base game alone is average, solid, and sound as an addition to any fantasy gamer's bookshelf... and even that of mainstream gamers who ordinarily don't have fantasy as their main diet. You will want some of the expansions eventually or the game becomes tedious when played too often.

RATING: 3
Talisman is one of those games I would love to love. The theme is great, the art is great... but there it stops.

The worst about it is that it's too random. Far too random. It plays like a complicated mix between snakes-and-ladders and ludo. Secondly, the bits are fiddly and easy to loose, and the numbers on the little plastic tokens are almost impossible to read. And the game takes so incredibly long to play and it takes far too much space on the table. 

So, while I might play this if someone REAAAAALLY wanted to... I probably won't ever play it again. The miniatures might be used for other purposes though.

RATING: 6
Talisman won't appeal to seasoned gamers; the roll and move mechanic may frustrate them quickly, and for good reason. It's more of a generically themed family game (provided the family is kind of geeky), and if you take it as such, it's enjoyable despite its poor design. There are little decisions to be made throughout as you build your character and push your luck. It's easy to learn and play, the art is well done, and it won't ask too much of your brain at the end of a hard day. Highly recommend the rules variant included with the game that shortens playing time.

RATING: 6
I'll confess, I would love to get back into RPGs, although unfortunately having a "life" makes it virtually impossible. I cut my gaming teeth on D&D like so many others, and while it would be pretty low on my list of RPG choices nowadays, I still have fond memories. Talisman manages to embody both the best (the thrill of beating a monster, the excitement of nabbing some cool loot) and the worst (that crazy backstabber just stole my gold!) of the experience. Overall, this was a blast to play!

Play again? You bet! We had to call the game off after about 90 minutes because of other commitments, and I could tell we'd barely scratched the surface, so this is a game that you would want to start only if you knew you had four or five uninterrupted hours available; and I could tell that the game would probably become repetitive if you found yourself stuck on the first "level" for too long. But it was a real blast of nostalgia, so I can see doing it again with the right set of people. I had played Descent at Origins 2009, and honestly I would pick Talisman over Descent any day.

Entra in un mondo fantastico di draghi e magia! In Talisman ti avventurerai in una cerca perigliosa, alla ricerca della leggendaria Corona del Comando. Potrai scegliere tra il guerriero, il prete, il mago o uno degli altri undici eroi dotati di poteri magici e abilità fisiche.
Ma il cammino che porta alla corona è rischioso. La leggenda narra che solo un favoloso Talismano possa proteggerti nelle lande che si trovano oltre il Portale del Potere. Inoltre, trovare un tale artefatto è un compito tutt’altro che semplice: mostri, trappole e oscura magia ti attendono in ogni turno di gioco. Quindi, affidati al tuo coraggio! Ne avrai bisogno per superare i tuoi avversari, per assicurarti la corona e forgiare il tuo destino!

Elenco elementi di gioco:
1 Tabellone
1 Regolamento
14 Schede personaggio
104 Carte Avventura

28 Carte Acquisto
4 Carte Talismano
4 Schede Rospo
4 Carte Allineamento
14 Miniature
6 Dadi
40 Segnalini Forza
40 Segnalini Astuzia
40 Segnalini Vitalità
30 Monete d'oro
36 Pedine Fato

RATING: 6
[Children's Game] It's a roll and move game with random encounter cards and equipment and levelling up. No tactics, no strategy, nothing to get in the way of an essential epic fantasy adventure. Whether you want that or not, Talisman is what it is: a well executed classic. Pure, simple, and easy. 

I really enjoy the first half of the game, but then it overstays its welcome when you get to the designed-for-frustration central ring. When the game transitions you from flipping cool and fun adventure cards, to literally just rolling dice over and over to see if you can hit a high target roll, it sort of stops being fun. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
Talisman is a classic for low-thought fun with of exploration and adventure. Don't look for strategy here; there's very little.
While the FFG version has made some good improvements (fate) and some great component upgrades (minis and plastic tokens, yay!), its still got a lot of flaws and confusing problems - some of which are almost 30 years old. Better in most ways than the original, thought its really silly that we have to use some of the same house rules we used to.

Ok, you can probably find this in the FAQ, but just to point out, craft/strength VALUE means the number printed on the card. We would never have gotten this without BGG: its poorly explained and completely counter-intuitive. (Base craft? Starting craft? Lots of better ways to say this).

The board is AWFUL. Seriously. Who in the world decided we needed a board twice the size of an average table with room for 20 people standing in each space?

RATING: 4
I've played this a few times now and it is just a terrible, terrible game. 

You spend three hours or so grinding out enough life, and skill points to be able to luck your way through the inner 2 rings. Unlucky rolling and you'll never get to a point where you can make it across (if you're going for craft) or if you do and you roll 'badly', you can end up being thrown all the way back to the beginning.

The only interesting aspect is when you time your dash to the inner rings (assuming you can roll the correct number to land where you need to), but even this is negated by the luck of the dice.

Just a terrible game that should be allowed to die quietly in the corner. I pity any new gamers that are introduced via this; they'd never come back.

RATING: 6.5
I recently found an old adventure game called Key to the Kingdom from an op shop. After perusing the rules, I mentally marked it off as a brainless roll-and-move adventure game with cool bits. Then one day, my son (aged 4) pointed it out in the game closet and wanted to give it a go. So we did with my daughter Jojo (aged 6) and to my surprise, we had a great time rolling dice and laughing at the random encounters. It was then when I decided that if we're going to play roll-and-move adventure games with cool bits, we might as well play one of the best ones out there, namely Talisman.

Story-telling is a must. Part of the fun was dramatically revealing encounters as they turn up and figuring out how events came about. Rather than just draw an Adventure Card to reveal a Witch and roll the die to determine what happens, Evan walked his dwarf through the path in the Woods till he came to the strange throne carved out from a tree-trunk (as depicted on the board). After sitting down on it to rest, an ugly Witch came out the trees screeching that it was her chair. However, after seeing how strong the Dwarf was, the Witch decides to give him a gift instead.

It was difficult to explain what 'Neutral' meant. The kids understood Good and Bad (Evil), but Neutral was a new concept to them. Simply saying that Neutral means 'sometimes Good and sometimes Evil' didn't help. On hindsight, perhaps demonstrating via an imaginary scale where Good is on one end, and Evil is on the other and Neutral is right in the middle might have been a better idea. Anyway, Evan was disturbed by the fact that his Dwarf was Neutral, so in the end we made his Dwarf a Good Dwarf by giving him the Good Alignment card.

The kids were surprisingly very co-operative to each other. When Jojo pulled out a new Spell card (Acquisition) that allowed her to steal an item from Evan, she expressed that she didn't want to hurt Evan; she wanted to help him. So I allowed her to ditch that Spell to draw another one. And there was a time when Evan found the Unicorn, and said that he'll pass it to his sister when they next meet because she loves Unicorns. As a parent, I'm happy that they're demonstrating brother-sister care for each other. As a gamer...? Ah well, I'm sure some cut-throat-ness will turn up in time
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
The be all and end all - no competition!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
I was on and off the fence about this game and it´s earlier editions (which I never played) for quite a while. But when I saw this game in Essen 2007, I was really taken with the quality of the components (I love the coins!) and as my girlfriend was also interested, I bought a copy.Our first two plays with two players were very good. There really is even less strategy involved than in Runebound but it also plays much faster. Even though there is little depth in this game, it is great fun and has relativley simple rules. Of course it is a dicefest to the extreme but I am quite fond of these. Compared to other RPG-Boardgames, it is definitly much weaker than Arkham Horror (because AH is less random, offers more choices and has even deeper theme but also takes much longer) and it is on about the same level as Runebound. While Runebound has more depth, more decisions and more detail it also has even less player interaction and especialy takes much longer. So it is a bit a question of mood. I guess with more than three players, Talisman always wins against Runebound as I *assume* that Talisman should be great and simple fun while I *know* that Runebound drags on forever with more than three players.

RATING: 7
I started playing Talisman back when I was about 10 years old (first edition). It's a fun little game, easy to understand and get non-board gamers into a fantasy world. I don't play this game with my more meta-strategy oriented friends as they find the luck to be too big of a factor in this game. Fantastic for casual play though, and I've gotten many non board gaming people into board games via Talisman. One of the main issues I have with the game is that it takes a very long time to complete, usually 3-4 hours when you have 5-6 players.
I've only ever once tried it with 8 players, never again.

RATING: 7
My best description of this game would be a combination of Monopoly and Munchkin. It is a game of dice-rolling chance to move your player around the board, but you get to gather weapons, magic items and spells to help you. You have to fight monsters and try to beat your opponents to the middle of the board. However, the middle of the board is where the worst dangers are, so don't go there until you are ready. I have the unrevised 4th Edition, which is not compatible with any expansions from any of the other versions. I was easily able to make minor modifications to the cards and board to "update" the game to the Revised 4th Edition. I just used a different game's parts for the Fate tokens. You can get a list of the changes online.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
I played Tales of the Arabian Nights a week prior to my first play of Talisman. Tales puts a lot of people off because there is little choice for the player. For me, Talisman is very similar, only with less of a story. 

Movement is via the roll of the die (although you do have a choice of clockwise or anti-clockwise). Much of the outcome is determined by a roll of the die, in the form of "roll the die to see what you find", "roll the die to see what you stole" or "roll the die to see if your armour protected you". With Tales, you get to pick from a number of choices (hide, fight, trick, etc). It may end up being just as random, but I find players feel a bit more involved in what is happening.  

At this point, I prefer Tales. It had people laughing more and they seemed to enjoy it more, if only for the novelty. Talisman is not bad. It even strikes a nostalgic chord, reminding me of games I played in my youth, but that's also the problem. It feels like something I've played before, played a lot, and outgrown.

RATING: 6
Definitely a dated game.  Roll and Move can be very frustrating when all you want to do is stop on one spot.  I really get a kick out of the exploration aspect though, I love just flipping a card and seeing what I run into, finding gear, leveling up.  This is like starter RPG for kids in that regard.  The part that sort of killed the game for me is the central area where the game drives into a rather dull traffic jam.  Especially when you FINALLY get to the top, and all you're doing is rolling a die on your turn and hoping that you can slowly kill every other player.

I bet the game is more fun when multiple people reach the center ring at once, but while that would offer more tension, I feel like it would also make the game last longer than it should.

RATING: 4
(One play) This game is extremely random and there is a lack of control in your actions and decision making, due to the roll and move and random cards. It feels like the game is playing you, and any decisions you make are usually arbitrary or obvious. Losing turns can be boring, and I can imagine turning into a toad to be extremely frustrating as it is very punishing (it didn't happen to me).

Luckily, the theme is very strong and I love fantasy. It did feel like an adventure, so I did have fun. I also won by kicking the troll's butt 10 times in a row with my monk, so that was awesome. I might play it again very occasionally.

If you're not a fantasy fan, avoid this game like the plague, as there is little else you'll find here.

Update: If you want a game that's random, play Tales of the Arabian Nights - it's infinitely more fun and entertaining.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
So much has been said of Talisman. Yes it is highly luck based. Yes it can stretch on for eons. Yes the board takes up exactly one square mile of table space. However, each expansion you add reduces luck factor and adds meaningful decisions and strategies. A few house rules greatly speed up the game and reduce frustrations. And... well nothing can be done about the gigantic boards.
Talisman itself is a pretty good game, but I'd have to admit expansions improve it quite a bit. It almost a labor of love because my god will you have cards to shuffle. You will spend hours thinking about how to delicately house rule a few things without changing the spirit of the game. But when everything comes together it really is a magical experience. AND it's the only game I can get my wife and casual game friends to play that smells vaguely D&D-ish.
This game is stronger in theme than anything I've played and writes a story of adventure each time. Count yourself lucky to play it or own it, because Fantasy Flight Games no longer publishes it due to Games Workshop withdrawing its license :(
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 9
A very good reprint of a classic game. Like many, I cut my teeth on the GW version and played this a lot when I was younger. Sure, the game is roll and move and the winner of the game is the one who gets the luckiest, but it is still fun if taken in light doses.

I liken it to gambling more than anything. You might spin the wheel and get the Runesword on your first turn - or you might draw a craft 12 demon that blasts you off the map. If you go into this one with the right mentality, you will have a good time.

RATING: 10
This is the game that started my love affair with "modern" board games back in the early nineties. 

Straight off the bat I was gripped with the mixed range of characters and their specific traits, how they bended the game for each player.

The levelling and development of the characters in order to attack the central goal, the crown, is a strategic evaluation / guessing game!

Then add on top of this a wealth of opponents, lovely artwork, items and events - not to mention the additional boards and expansion packs and you might get an idea why this is one of my favourite things

Nowadays, the game isn't as well regarded (my wife cannot see the merit involved) but due to my sentiment it will always remain golden.

RATING: 1
This game basically comes down to simple die rolls and luck of the draw whichever cards you happen to get, and then fighting with everybody else over things nobody has any control over. You can spend hours building your character then meet something that can simple remove all everybody's fate tokens, even if you didn't draw it, or are force to point some item or spell at someone and, because you dared to point it at the obvious leader with a vast pile of STUFF, they turn around and obliterate all your progress easily. 

My friend put it as such: "It's too much like real life", and really, I'm inclined to agree. The game will slowly spoonfeed you upgrades and life and strength and such only to pull it out from under you whenever it feels like it. Unless you happen to be lucky enough to be a character with a completely broken skill and can get so much stuff you can't manage it any more.

If you have a good group then you may be able to get laughs out of each others misfortune and make light of the situations, but if you have such a group there are much better games you could be playing.

I have two friends who want us to play this occasionally for nostalgia purposes. I think their nostalgia is where this ought to stay.

RATING: 7
This score is higher than it probably should.. but this is a sort of "guilty pleasure" game and an old classic. Yes, it's flawed, especially compared to more modern titles.. the downtimes are terrible, interaction minimal, basically anyone can play solo, and with many people it becomes a drag. It's also dependant on luck and dice rolls (although some strategic planning can be involved). Still - it's simple, works surprisingly great as a tablet game for travel (I think it gave this game a new life, actually), and the fun of choosing and developing your character (albeit in too random way), using its powers, collecting items is still there. It's just a mindless, fun, adventure game with really easy, clear rules. Lower the score if you never played it as a kid and already played some more advanced titles, though.

RATING: 6
I like Talisman as a semi-mindless casual game. There are enough decisions and interaction that it doesn't feel like Candyland, while in the meantime you have a nicely thematic set of cards to play with. The primary downside to the game is that it's very imbalanced (lol Assassin. lol Ghoul), but this is fixed just by giving two character cards to every player, or by taking out all of the OP cards and having a "gimp game."

The games can sometimes drag on too long, so make sure you allow people to concede when it's pretty clear who the winner will be.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
I shied away from Talisman for a long time because everything I had heard about it seemed bad. Roll and move, monopoly board, completely random, too long, etc. I enjoy adventure games, but hate role-playing proper, so instead, I sought out games like Runebound and Descent to get my adventuring fix. At some point, I decided to give Talisman a try simply because the arguments between its supporters and detractors intrigued me. How can a game that is so obviously bad, have so much love directed toward it?

I came away from my plays with a couple of thoughts. First of all, I'll talk about the randomness. Yes, it is almost completely random from start to finish. You roll dice to randomly determine where you can go, you draw a random card to see what happens when you get there and finally you roll a die to see if you succeed or fail. That does indeed sound terrible, but can you look at a game like Runebound and honestly say that it does it any better?

In Runebound you roll a handful of dice and move by spending dice that show symbols that match the terrain hexes on the board. You are rolling dice to randomly determine where you can move. That's not different, it is actually performing the exact same function but adding in unnecessary complication. After you get where you are going, you draw a random card and do what it says. Sometimes you roll a die to see what happens to you. It's exactly the same, right?

Combat in Talisman is a single die roll. Runebound forces a few die rolls (still using randomness to completely determine the results of combat) to resolve its combat. Is this actually better? I don't think so...

My point is that the supposed "more strategic" gameplay of Runebound is an illusion. Talisman provides the exact same decision points and delivers them in far easier and more intuitive fashion. For that reason alone, I think Talisman might just be a better game despite its old-school design philosophy and dated engine.

RATING: 3
I quite dislike this game. It feels like the game auto-plays itself for about 40% already. You roll a die, see when you move. Roll a die to see if you beat a creature. Draw a random card to see if you get to beat up a chump, get beaten up yourself by a dragon or encounter a special location.

I have to admit, I like the idea behind the Encounter deck, where shops can pop-up potentially anywhere or that you can encounter monsters. 

But I severly dislike fighting monsters. It feels incredibly uninspired (1d6 + some bonuses vs 1d6 + some bonuses) and dull. And as you seem to be doing quite some fighting to power up your character, it feels like a grind. A multiplayer grindfest I might add!

I wouldn't have minded it so much if the game would take about 30m or so. But it can take up hours! Multiple hours of just hoping to have more good rolls getting more usefull encounters than your opponents.

It's a shame though as I can see potential in a game like this. But the implementation of the 'Talisman idea' in the actual game feels lacking to me.

RATING: 6
I used to really like this, but recently I really can't bring myself to suggest it over the other games we have. 

I mean, it's fun to play with the right people, but I found that there's always other games that I'd rather ask after (like Lords of Waterdeep).

Essentially, I like the events and the idea that you have to climb your way up to the goal in the middle of the board, but if you're unlucky you can find yourself being a wall flower while the other players have fun simply because you keep getting stuff that does't help you progress. 

If there was a similar game where you get tons of event cards and dragons to slay but the things that you do had more bearing on how much you level up, I think it would become my favourite game ever but as it is sometimes it's really frustrating and it doesn't necessarily feel like I could have done anything to get a much better result.

RATING: 8
Regarding FFG version:

Crud! I had no idea how much cooler the game would be with minis, but I love them! The new larger character cards are also great.

My nitpicks are, first, that FFG only gave you 30 gold coins compared to the 60 from BI - plus the latter are inked! I am glad I could swap the 30 FFG gold coins for the 60 inked gold coins from the BI version though. Secondly, that the cards are now even smaller and the art is too good to be cropped so much.

Fate definitely improves the game IMO. I have a lot of fun with it, and feel like it balances out some of the characters.

This is my 4-year old daughters favorite game. (Edit: This same daughter is now 9, and still loves Talisman.)

RATING: 6
Talisman is a fun game of randomness. It's easy to get upset with the game or other players while playing. Luck is a huge factor in the game, it can hose you for awhile or it can give you a major head start on the other players. 

Each of the expansions add so much to the game with all the new spells, adventure cards and characters to play as. 

This makes an excellent game to sit around and BS while laughing at someone elses misfortune or even get upset and seek revenge on another player. Sometimes other players will need to be put in check because that was your Rune Sword they took and now its Arse Smacking Time.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
After playing this game a few times to adequately assess this rating, my enjoyment was much lower than I initially expected.  Each session was either way too long or too short and worst of all, it is entirely random.  No need to strategize whatsoever as card draws and dice rolls determine everything!  Pitiful is a very good word for a game that seemed to have much more potential.

I didn't play the game with a large group, but quite honestly, I would fear that it would drag on even further and quite possibly receive an even lower rating from me.

Fantasy Flight Games did a great job with the production quality, as expected, but the game falls too flat on all other accounts.

I find it comparable in strategy and complexity to Monopoly... maybe even The Game of Life.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Type: Adventure
Number of Players: 2-6
Sub-Type: Roll and Move, Dice Rolling, Variable Player Powers
Game Flow: (2/4) 
Gameplay: (4/6)

Game Length: Average (Long w/out Variant)
Game Balance: Average
Strategy: Average
Luck Factor: Average (High w/out Variant)
Replay Value: High

Suggested Variants: 
a) Challenge and Reward Decks - Split the Adventure Cards into Challenge (1-3) and Reward Decks (4-6).
b) Scaling Experience - The Number of Strength/Craft required when turning in Monster Trophies is equal to the Character's current stat value.
c) Reduced Random Movement - Move up to the Die Roll resolving any Hazardous Locations before continuing on with Movement. Players must stop on any Monsters they land on.
d) Select From Multiple Characters - Reduce the Character pool to 18 Characters (Removing imbalanced Characters). Deal a number of characters equal to the number of players plus one. Determine first player, who selects the character they wish to play. Place a fate token on all characters not selected. Players continue clockwise choosing characters, taking any fate tokens that may be present.
e) High Power Decks - Removed any cards that slow down play from the Spells and Adventure Decks

RATING: 9
A wonderful new version of Talisman. Not the same nostalgical feel as the 1st/2nd edition, as the illustrations are not the same, otherwise exactly the same game. Good cards, rather nice materials (though there is no need to have numbers on the counters, just use all the counters as a "1"), very nice board. Feels modern while the old version keeps its weird flavour. Same rating, though.

RATING: 2.5
Fourth edition of the old fantasy themed roll and move game. You are a hero who tries to get to the middle of the map to claim the crown of command.
You could die on your first turn by finding the mightiest enemy in the game or still be at 0 experience points 60 minutes into the game because you haven't found a single enemy. Everything in this game is based on pure luck and you have two choices per turn - at most!
